===== PAGE 25 =====

! 
23 
A typical sacrifice of the d6-pawn, also seen in the Averbakh Variation. 
Worse is 8 ... b5 9.cxb5 a6 10.Nd2, transposing into the game I.Sokolov-Nijboer, 
Breda 2000, examined above under the move order 6 ... b5 7.cxb5 a6. He could keep 
the d6-pawn by 8 ... Nh5, but here the knight is not so well placed: 9.Be3 eS 
10.dxe6 (if White does not take en passant, then Black manoeuvres along the lines 
of variation B2a, and it is quite unclear where the white bishop would stand better 
- on e3 or d2) 10 ... Bxe6 11.Qd2 Kh7 12.Rd1 Qb6 13.Be2 Nc6 
14.0-0 Rad8 {Kanep-Nataf, Dresden 2007) 15.h3 Rfe8 16.Rfe1 with a small 
advantage on account of the superior structure. 
9.dxe6 Bxe6 (26) 
26 
Theca sau khi 9 ... Bxe6 
10.Bxd6 
On 10.Qxd6 a good reply is 10 ... Qa5 11.Qd2 Nc6 12.Bd3 gS 13.Bg3 Rfe8 14.0-0 
Rad8 15.Qe2 NhS with the initiative, whilst if 10.Gl.d2, then 10 ... Qb6 (but not 
10 ... Qa5? 11.Bxh6 Bxh6 12.Qxh6 Nxe4, which is refuted by 13.Bd3! Nxc3 
14.0-0) 11.0-0-0 Kh7, and after 12.Bxd6 there is 12 ... Rd8 13.e5 Ne8. 
10 ... Re8 ll.Be2 
Black should not fear the loss of a second pawn: 11.Bxc5 (Lengyei-Kavalek, Tel 
Aviv 1964) 11 ... Qa5 12.b4 Qa6 13.Rc1 Nbd7 14.Be3 {14.Bd4 Bxc4 15.b5 Qe63 ) 
14 ... Rac8 15.b5 QaS= Black has already completed his development 
and the question of regaining the pawns on c4 and e4 can be regarded as answered. 
ll ... Qb6 (27) 
A move with many plans: the queen attacks the b2-pawn, defends the pawn on 
cS and also frees d8 for the rook. The other popular reply, 11 ... Nc6 12.0-0 Nd4 
13.e5 Nd7, leads after simplifications to an endgame where Black is fighting 
for a draw.

trl hoan phat trien Ma "g1". Chfnh dieu nay cho Trang rat nhieu ll)'a chon tot, va
